Question: The average (arithmetic mean) of the weight of 10 vehicles is 12.2 tons. The average weight of the group of vehicles increased by 2.6 tons after a new heavy duty truck was added to the group? What is the weight in tons of the heavy duty truck?
Choices:
  A: 40.8
  B: 41.6
  C: 42.2
  D: 43.5
  E: 44.8
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  The average of a set of numbers is their sum divided by the number of elements in the set.
  We can use the formula (sum of the original weights + weight of the new truck)/(number of vehicles + 1) = new average weight of the group.
  We know the original average weight and the new average weight after adding the new truck.
Thought:
  Let the weight of the new truck be x.
  According to the problem, (sum of original weights)/10 = 12.2, so sum of original weights = 122.
  After adding the new truck, (sum of original weights + x)/11 = 14.8 (12.2+2.6).

Topic: Math
Question: 10kg of a mixture contains 30% sand and 70% clay. In order to make the mixture contain equal quantities of clay and sand how much of the mixture is to be removed and replaced with pure sand?
Choices:
  A: 10/7
  B: 20/7
  C: 30/7
  D: 40/7
  E: 50/7
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  The mixture contains 30% sand and 70% clay.
  The amount of sand and clay in the mixture are not equal.
  A portion of the mixture needs to be removed and replaced with pure sand.
Thought:
  Let the amount of mixture to be removed be x kg.
  The amount of sand in the mixture before removal is 30% of 10kg, which is 3kg.
  The amount of clay in the mixture before removal is 70% of 10kg, which is 7kg.
  After removing x kg of mixture, there will be (10 - x) kg of mixture left.
  Let y kg of pure sand be added to the remaining mixture.
  The amount of sand in the remaining mixture will be (3 - 0.3x + y) kg.
  The amount of clay in the remaining mixture will be (7 - 0.7x) kg.
  We want the amount of sand and clay to be equal after the replacement.
  So, (3 - 0.3x + y) = (7 - 0.7x).
  Simplifying the equation, we get 0.4x - y = 4.
  We also know that the amount of mixture removed and replaced with pure sand is x + y kg.
  We need to find the value of x + y.
  To solve for x + y, we need to find the values of x and y.
  There are many possible values of x and y that satisfy the equation 0.4x - y = 4.
  For example, if we let x = 5 and y = 2, then 0.4x - y = 0.2, which is not equal to 4.
  Therefore, we need to use a different approach to solve the problem.
  One approach is to use the fact that the amount of clay in the mixture is twice the amount of sand after the replacement.
  So, (7 - 0.7x) = 2(3 - 0.3x + y).
  Simplifying the equation, we get 1.1x - 2y = 1.
  Now, we have two equations with two unknowns:
    0.4x - y = 4
    1.1x - 2y = 1
  Solving the system of equations, we get x = 20/7 and y = 10/7.
  Therefore, the amount of mixture to be removed and replaced with pure sand is 20/7 + 10/7 = 30/7 kg.
Answer: Answer("C")

  The final mixture needs to have equal quantities of sand and clay. So, the percentage of sand in the final mixture will be 50%.

    0.3(10 - x) + x = 0.5(10)

    3 - 0.3x + x = 5
    0.7x = 2
    x = 20/7
  Therefore, we need to remove and replace 20/7 kg of the mixture with pure sand.

Question: Find the total no. of distinct bike no.'s that can beformed using 2 letters followed by 2 no.'s. How many letters need to be distinct?
Choices:
  A: 74453
  B: 64543
  C: 74325
  D: 65000
  E: 97656
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  To find the total number of distinct bike numbers that can be formed using 2 letters followed by 2 numbers, we need to find:
  - The number of ways to choose the first letter (26 options)
  - The number of ways to choose the second letter (26 options)
  - The number of ways to choose the first number (10 options)
  - The number of ways to choose the second number (10 options)
  Then, we need to multiply these numbers together to get the total number of distinct bike numbers.
Thought:
  There are 26 options for the first letter and 26 options for the second letter.
  There are 10 options for the first number and 10 options for the second number.
  Therefore, the total number of distinct bike numbers that can be formed is:
  26 * 26 * 10 * 10 = 67600
  Each letter needs to be distinct, so there are 2 distinct letters.
  The answer is 2.
Criticism:
  Your answer for the number of distinct bike numbers is correct.
  However, the question is asking how many letters need to be distinct, not how many distinct bike numbers can be formed.

Response 1:
Knowledge:
  To find the total number of distinct bike numbers that can be formed using 2 letters followed by 2 numbers, we can use the multiplication principle of counting, which states that if there are m ways to do one thing and n ways to do another thing, then there are m x n ways to do both things.
  There are 26 letters in the English alphabet and 10 digits from 0 to 9.
Thought:
  The first two characters of the bike number can be any 2 letters from the English alphabet. There are 26 choices for the first letter and 26 choices for the second letter. Therefore, there are 26 x 26 = 676 ways to choose the first two characters.
  The last two characters of the bike number can be any 2 digits from 0 to 9. There are 10 choices for the first digit and 10 choices for the second digit. Therefore, there are 10 x 10 = 100 ways to choose the last two characters.
  By the multiplication principle, the total number of distinct bike numbers that can be formed is 676 x 100 = 67,600.
  All the letters need to be distinct, as we are choosing two letters, not two sets of letters. 
  Therefore, two different letters can be chosen in 26 × 25 (650) ways.

Topic: Math
Question: What will be the cost of gardening 1-metre – broad boundary around a rectangular plot having perimeter of 340 metres at the rate of 10 per square metre?
Choices:
  A: 3400
  B: 1700
  C: 3440
  D: Cannot be determined
  E: None of these
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  The perimeter of a rectangle is found by adding the lengths of all four sides.
  The formula for the perimeter of a rectangle is P = 2(l + w), where P is the perimeter, l is the length, and w is the width.
  To find the area of the rectangle, multiply the length by the width: A = lw.
Thought:
  Let's first find the length and width of the rectangular plot.
  The perimeter of a rectangle is the sum of all its sides.
  So, 2(l + w) = 340, which simplifies to l + w = 170.
  We cannot determine the individual values of l and w from this information.
  However, we do not need to know the individual values of l and w to find the cost of gardening a 1-meter boundary around the rectangle.
  The width of the boundary will be 1 meter on either side, so the new length and width of the rectangle will be (l + 2) and (w + 2), respectively.
  The area of the boundary will be the difference between the area of the larger rectangle and the smaller rectangle: (l + 2)(w + 2) - lw.
  So, the cost of gardening the 1-meter boundary will be the area of the boundary multiplied by the cost per square meter, which is 10.
  Therefore, the total cost will be 10[(l + 2)(w + 2) - lw].
  We cannot determine the individual values of l and w, but we can determine the value of (l + 2)(w + 2) - lw.
  Expanding this expression, we get lw + 2l + 2w + 4 - lw = 2(l + w) + 4 = 2(170) + 4 = 344.
  So, the total cost will be 10(344) = 3440.
  The answer is C: 3440.
Criticism:
  There are no apparent flaws in the facts, logic, or reasoning used to solve the problem.

  We are given that perimeter of the plot is 340 meters.
  340 = 2(length + breadth)
  length + breadth = 170
  Let's assume the breadth of the rectangular plot is x meters.
  Therefore, the length of the rectangular plot would be (170 - x) meters.
  We need to find the cost of gardening a 1-meter wide strip around the rectangular plot.
  The area of the strip's outer rectangle would be (length+2)*(breadth+2) and the area of the plot's rectangle would be length*breadth.
  The area of the strip would be the difference between the area of the outer rectangle and the plot's rectangle.
  Area of the rectangular plot = length * breadth = (170 - x) * x = 170x - x^2
  Area of the strip = (length+2)*(breadth+2) - length * breadth
                     = (170 - x + 2) * (x + 2) - (170x - x^2)
                     = 174x - x^2 + 344
  Therefore, the total area that needs to be gardened would be the area of the strip + the area of the plot:
  Total Area = Area of Strip + Area of Plot
             = 174x - x^2 + 344 + 170x - x^2
             = 344x - 2x^2 + 344
  Cost of gardening = area of garden x cost per square meter
                    = (344x - 2x^2 + 344) * 10
                    = 3440x - 20x^2 + 3440
  To find x, we can use the fact that length + breadth = 170
  We know that breadth = x meters and length = (170 - x) meters
  So, we can write the equation as:
  x + (170 - x) = 170
  Solving this equation gives us x = 85.
  Substituting this value of x in the expression for the cost of gardening gives:
  Cost of gardening = 3440(85) - 20(85^2) + 3440
                    = 292400
Therefore, the cost of gardening would be $292400.

  The area of the garden would be (L+2)*(B+2) - L*B.
  Simplifying the area of the garden gives 2L + 2B + 4.
  The cost of gardening would be the area of the garden times the rate, which is 10.
  Therefore, the cost would be 10 * (2L + 2B + 4).
  However, we still need to find the values of L and B.
  We know that L + B = 170, but we cannot determine the individual values of L and B.
  Therefore, the answer is D: Cannot be determined.
Criticism:
  The solution is correct.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 9:
Knowledge:
  Perimeter of a rectangle = 2 * (length + breadth)
  To find the cost of gardening, we need to know the area of the rectangular plot and the area of the plot after a 1-meter boundary is added.
Thought:
  Let's say the length of the rectangular plot is L and the breadth is B.
  According to the problem, 2(L+B) = 340, so L + B = 170.
  Let's say the length of the plot after adding a 1-meter boundary is L1 and the breadth is B1.
  Then, L1 = L + 2 and B1 = B + 2 (adding 1 meter on each side)
  The area of the original rectangular plot = L * B
  The area of the plot after adding the 1-meter boundary = L1 * B1
  The area of the boundary = (L1 * B1) - (L * B)
  The cost of gardening the boundary = Area of the boundary * Rate per square meter
  Solving for the values:
  L + B = 170
  L1 = L + 2
  B1 = B + 2
  Area of the rectangular plot = L * B
  Area of the plot after adding the 1-meter boundary = (L+2) * (B+2)
  Area of the boundary = (L+2)*(B+2) - L*B
  Cost of gardening = (L+2)*(B+2) - L*B * 10
  Simplifying the expression, we get:
  Cost of gardening = 10*(2*L + 2*B + 4)
  Cost of gardening = 10*(2*(L + B) + 4)
  Cost of gardening = 10*(2*170 + 4)
  Cost of gardening = 10*(344)
  Cost of gardening = 3440
Therefore, the cost of gardening 1-metre – broad boundary around a rectangular plot having perimeter of 340 metres at the rate of 10 per square metre is 3440.
The answer is C: 3440.

### Temperature: 8.0 | Problem 90 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Calculate the percentage gain of a merchant who purchased 90 kg of oranges for Rs. 450 and sold the whole lot at the rate of Rs. 7.50 per kg.
Choices:
  A: 50 %
  B: 60 %
  C: 55 %
  D: 70 %
  E: 58%
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  Percentage gain is calculated as ((profit/cost price)*100).
  Cost price is the price at which the merchant purchased the oranges.
  Profit is the difference between the selling price and the cost price.
  The merchant purchased 90 kg of oranges for Rs. 450.
  The selling price of each kg of orange is Rs. 7.50.
Thought:
  The total selling price of 90 kg of oranges is (90 * Rs. 7.50) = Rs. 675.
  The cost price of 90 kg of oranges is Rs. 450.
  The profit made by the merchant is (Rs. 675 - Rs. 450) = Rs. 225.
  Percentage gain is ((225/450)*100) = 50%.
  Therefore, the percentage gain of the merchant is 50%.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  Percentage gain = (Profit / Cost Price) * 100
  Profit = Selling Price - Cost Price
Thought:
  Cost price of 90 kg of oranges = Rs. 450
  Cost price per kg = 450/90 = Rs. 5
  Selling price = 90 * 7.5 = Rs. 675
  Profit = Selling price - Cost price = Rs. 675 - Rs. 450 = Rs. 225
  Percentage gain = (Profit / Cost Price) * 100 = (225 / 450) * 100 = 50%
  Therefore, the percentage gain is 50%.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 2:

  Therefore, the percentage gain is 50%.

  Percentage Gain = (Profit / Cost Price) × 100%

- Profit is the difference between the Selling Price and the Cost Price.
- Selling Price is the amount received by selling the goods.
Thought:

- The Cost Price of 1 kg of oranges is Rs. 450 / 90 kg = Rs. 5.
- The merchant sold the oranges at the rate of Rs. 7.50 per kg.
- The Selling Price of 1 kg of oranges is Rs. 7.50.
- Profit per kg of oranges = Selling Price - Cost Price = Rs. 7.50 - Rs. 5 = Rs. 2.50.
- Total Profit = Profit per kg × No. of kg = Rs. 2.50/kg × 90 kg = Rs. 225.
- Percentage Gain = (Profit / Cost Price) × 100% = (Rs. 225 / Rs. 450) × 100% = 50%.
- Therefore, the merchant had a 50% gain.

Topic: Math
Question: There is well of depth 30m and frog is at bottom of the well. He jumps 3m up one day and falls back 2m down the same day. How many days will it take for the frog to come out of the well?
Choices:
  A: 25 days
  B: 26 days
  C: 27 days
  D: 28 days
  E: 29 days
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  The frog jumps 3m up and falls 2m down each day.
  The well is 30m deep.
  The frog needs to reach the top of the well to come out.
Thought:
  On the first day, the frog jumps 3m up and is 27m from the top.
  On the first night, the frog falls 2m down and is 29m from the top.
  On the second day, the frog jumps 3m up and is 26m from the top.
  On the second night, the frog falls 2m down and is 28m from the top.
  Continuing this pattern, the frog will reach the top of the well on the 28th day.
  Therefore, the answer is D: 28 days.
Criticism:
  There is no criticism to this solution.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Knowledge: 
  The frog jumps 3m up and falls back 2m down every day.
  The well is 30m deep.
Thought:
  The frog jumps 3m up and falls back 2m down every day.
  Thus, the frog covers 1m of height every day.
  Therefore, it will take 30 days for the frog to reach the top of the well.
  However, on the 30th day, the frog will jump 3m up and will reach the top of the well, and will not fall back 2m down.
  Therefore, the frog takes 29 days to come out of the well.
  The answer is E: 29 days.
Criticism: 
  There is no flaw in the reasoning.
Action: Answer("E")
Response 2:
Knowledge:
  The frog jumps 3 meters up and falls back 2 meters down, which means it makes a net gain of 1 meter every day.
  The well has a depth of 30 meters.
Thought:
  The frog makes a net gain of 1 meter every day, and the depth of the well is 30 meters.
  Therefore, the frog will take 30 days to come out of the well.
  However, the frog jumps up on the 30th day, but it doesn't fall back down. Therefore, the frog comes out of the well on the morning of the 30th day.
  Therefore, the answer is A: 30 - 1 = 29 days.
Criticism:
  There is no criticism to this solution.
Action: Answer("E")

  The depth of the well is 30m.
  The frog jumps up 3m and falls back 2m on the same day.

  Therefore, at the end of the first day, the frog is 29m below the top of the well.
  On the second day, the frog jumps up 3m and falls back 2m again, so the net distance covered is 1m.
  Therefore, at the end of the second day, the frog is 28m below the top of the well.
  In general, on the nth day, the frog will be 30 - (n-1) + 1 = 31 - n meters below the top of the well.
  Therefore, the frog will come out of the well on the day when 31 - n = 0, which is the 31st day.
  Therefore, it will take 31 days for the frog to come out of the well.

Question: Joe's age, Joe's sister's age and Joe’s fathers age sums up to 100. When Joe is as old as his father, Joe's sister will be twice as old as now. When Joe is as old as his father then his father is twice as old as when his sister was as old as her father. Find the age of Joe's father?

  B: 48
  C: 50
  D: 55
  E: 58
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  Let's assume that Joe's age is 'J', Joe’s sister's age is 'S' and Joe's father's age is 'F'.
  From the problem statement, we know that "Joe's age, Joe's sister's age and Joe’s fathers age sums up to 100". So, J + S + F = 100.
  We also know that "When Joe is as old as his father, Joe's sister will be twice as old as now". This means that S + (F-J) = 2S => F = S+J.
  Finally, we know that "When Joe is as old as his father then his father is twice as old as when his sister was as old as her father". This means that (S+J) - J = 2((S+J)-S) => S+J-J = 2S+2J-2S => J = S.
Thought:
  From "Joe's age, Joe's sister's age and Joe’s fathers age sums up to 100" and "F = S+J", we can substitute J with S in the first equation and get S + 2J = 100.
  Combining this with J = S, we get 3S = 100 => S = 33.33 (approx).
  Therefore, J = 33.33 (approx) and F = S+J = 66.67 (approx).
  But, we need to find the age of Joe's father as an integer.
  Since F is twice of J, we can check the answer choices for a multiple of 2 in the given options.
  Option (B) 48 is twice of 24 (which is close to 33).
  So, let's assume that Joe's age is 24 and Joe’s sister's age is also 24.
  From J + S + F = 100, we get F = 52.
  Now, let's verify if this satisfies the second condition too.
  When Joe is as old as his father, Joe's sister will be twice as old as now. This means when J = F, S = 48.
  At this point, Joe's father is twice as old as when his sister was as old as her father.
  When S = F/2 = 26, J = 26 too. (Since J=S)
  Therefore, F = 52 satisfies all the given conditions.
  So, the age of Joe's father is 52.

### Temperature: 8.0 | Problem 94 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Christopher and Jonathan were having bets. They decide that a coin will be flipped twenty times and each time it turns heads, Christopher will give $2 to Jonathan and each time it turns out to be Tails, Jonathan will give 3$ to Christopher. After flipping for twenty times none of the both won or lost any amount.
How many times did the coin landed on Heads ?
Choices:
  A: 10
  B: 23
  C: 16
  D: 18
  E: 12
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  In each flip, the probability of getting Heads is 0.5 (assuming a fair coin).
  Christopher gives $2 to Jonathan each time Heads is flipped.
  Jonathan gives $3 to Christopher each time Tails is flipped.
  The total number of flips is 20.
Thought:
  Let's assume that the coin landed on Heads x times and on Tails y times.
  We know that x + y = 20 (since there are 20 flips in total).
  We also know that Christopher gave Jonathan $2 x times, so Christopher gave away a total of 2x dollars.
  Similarly, Jonathan gave Christopher $3 y times, so Jonathan gave away a total of 3y dollars.
  Since none of them won or lost any amount, we have:
  2x = 3y  --> 2x/3 = y
  Substituting y into the equation x + y = 20, we get:
  x + 2x/3 = 20  --> 5x/3 = 20  --> x = 12
  Therefore, the coin landed on Heads 12 times.
  The answer is E: 12.
Criticism: 
  The calculation and reasoning are correct.
Action: Answer("E")
Response 1:
Knowledge: 
  Christopher will give $2 to Jonathan for each Head result.
  Jonathan will give $3 to Christopher for each Tail result.
  After 20 flips, neither Christopher nor Jonathan won or lost any amount.
Thought: 
  Let's assume that the coin landed on heads x times out of 20 times, and so it must have landed on Tails (20-x) times.
  Christopher will give $2 to Jonathan x times.
  Jonathan will give $3 to Christopher (20-x) times.
  The total amount won by Christopher is $2x and the total amount lost by Christopher is $3(20-x).
  Since neither player won or lost any amount, then the total amount won must be equal to the total amount lost.
  2x = 3(20-x)
  2x = 60-3x
  5x = 60
  x = 12
  Therefore, the coin landed on Heads 12 times.
  The answer is E: 12.

### Temperature: 8.0 | Problem 95 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Kevin drove from A to B at a constant speed of 70 mph. Once he reached B, he turned right around with pause, and returned to A at a constant speed of 90 mph. Exactly 3 hours before the end of his trip, he was still approaching B, only 70 miles away from it. What is the distance between A and B?
Choices:
  A: 180
  B: 90
  C: 270
  D: 360
  E: None of the above
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  - Kevin drove at 70 mph from A to B and 90 mph from B back to A.
  - Kevin took a break at point B before returning to A.
  - Kevin was 70 miles away from point B 3 hours before his trip ended.
Thought: 
  Let's call the distance between A and B "d". 
  Kevin drove from A to B and then back to A, covering a total distance of 2d. 
  Let's call the time it took Kevin to travel from A to B "t" (in hours). 
  Since he drove at a constant speed, we can use the formula: distance = rate x time, to find t. 
  We know that distance = d, rate = 70, and time = t, so we get d = 70t. 
  Similarly, let's call the time it took Kevin to travel from B to A "u" (in hours). 
  Again, we can use the formula: distance = rate x time, to find u. 
  We know that distance = d, rate = 90, and time = u, so we get d = 90u. 
  We also know that Kevin was 70 miles away from B 3 hours before his trip ended. 
  This means that he had already traveled a total of (2d - 70) miles at that point. 
  We can use this information to set up an equation: 
  (2d - 70) = 70t + 90u - 210 (since he had 3 hours left and was traveling at 70 mph) 
  Simplifying this equation, we get: 
  2d = 70t + 90u + 140 
  We can substitute d = 70t and d = 90u from earlier to get: 
  70t = 90u + 140 
  Solving for u, we get: 
  u = (7/9)t - (14/9) 
  We know that Kevin's total travel time was t + u + 3, so we can substitute u and simplify to get: 
  t + (7/9)t - (14/9) + 3 = (16/9)t + (23/9) 
  Simplifying further, we get: 
  (7/9)t = (68/9) 
  Solving for t, we get t = 68/7 hours. 
  Finally, we can use d = 70t to find the distance between A and B: 
  d = 70(68/7) = 680 
  So the distance between A and B is 680 miles.

  - The formula for total time of the trip is `time = distance / rate`.
  - Since the distance from A to B is the same as the distance from B to A, we can assume that the total time for the round trip is twice the time from A to B.
Thought:
  - Let's call the distance from A to B "d".
  - The time it takes Kevin to drive from A to B is `time = distance / rate = d / 70`.
  - The time it takes Kevin to drive from B to A is `time = distance / rate = d / 90`.
  - The total time for the round trip is `2 * (d / 70 + d / 90) = 2 * (9d / 630 + 7d / 630) = 32d / 315`.
  - We know that 3 hours before the end of the trip, Kevin is 70 miles away from B, so he has driven a total of `d - 70` miles at that point.
  - We also know that he has `32d / 315 - 3` hours left in his trip.
  - Using the formula `distance = rate * time`, we can set up the following equation: `d - 70 = 90 * (32d / 315 - 3)`.
  - Solving for d, we get `d = 360`.

  - Kevin's one-way trip from A to B at 70 mph took t1 hours.
  - Therefore, t1 = x/70.
  - Kevin's return trip from B to A at 90 mph took t2 hours.
  - Therefore, t2 = x/90.
  - Total time of the trip is given as 3 hours less than t1 + t2.
  - Total time of the trip is ((x/70) + (x/90)) - 3.
  - The total distance of the trip is 2x miles.
  - We also know that, 70 miles away from B, exactly 3 hours before the end of the trip, which means there is (t1 + t2 - 3) = ((x/70) + (x/90) - 3) hours left in the trip.
  - Using the formula for the total distance, we get; 
  total distance = total time * total speed.
  2x = ((x/70) + (x/90) - 3) * (70 + 90)
  2x = (9x + 7x - 1890)
  2x = 16x - 1890
  14x = 1890
  x = 135
  Therefore, the distance between A and B is 135 miles.

  D = 330 * (D/70)
  D = 4.5 * D

### Temperature: 8.0 | Problem 97 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: An organization decided to raise Rs. 6 lakh by collecting equal contribution from each of its employees. If each of them had contributed Rs. 60 extra, the contribution would have been Rs. 6.24 lakh. How many employees are there in that organization?
Choices:
  A: 300
  B: 200
  C: 400
  D: 100
  E: 500
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Let's assume the number of employees in the organization to be 'n'.
  The organization wants to raise Rs. 6 lakh by collecting the same amount from each employee, so the contribution of each employee would be Rs. 600000/n.
  If each employee had to contribute Rs. 60 extra, then the new contribution of each employee would be Rs. (600000 + 60n)/n.
  The total contribution after the increase is Rs. 6.24 lakh.
Thought:
  The contribution per person will be (600000 + 60n)/n.
  And the total number of employees will be the total amount raised divided by the contribution per person.
  So, equating both and solving for 'n':
  (600000 + 60n)/n = 624000/n
  600000 + 60n = 624000
  60n = 24000
  n = 400
  Therefore, there are 400 employees in the organization.
  The answer is C: 400.
Criticism:
  There is no flaw in the facts, logic, and reasoning applied to this problem.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  Let's assume there are 'n' employees in the organization.
  The organization needs to raise Rs. 6 lakh by collecting equal contribution from each of its employees, so each employee will contribute Rs. 6 lakh / n.
  If each employee had contributed Rs. 60 extra, the new contribution from each employee would be Rs. 6.24 lakh / n.
Thought:
  Let's assume that the contribution required from each employee is 'x' rupees.
  Then, we can write an equation as:
  n * x = 600,000  (because each employee needs to contribute 'x' amount, and there are 'n' employees in total)
  And, we can write another equation as:
  n * (x + 60) = 624,000  (because each employee would contribute 'x+60' amount, and there are 'n' employees in total)
  We can simplify the second equation by distributing 'n' and simplifying:
  n*x + n*60 = 624,000
  We know from the first equation that n*x = 600,000, so we can substitute that in the second equation:
  600,000 + n*60 = 624,000
  n*60 = 24,000
  n = 400
  Therefore, there are 400 employees in that organization.
Answer: Answer("C")

  6,00,000 + 60x = 6,24,000
  60x = 24,000

    N*X + N*60 = 6,24,000

    6,00,000 + N*60 = 6,24,000
  We can simplify this equation:
    N*60 = 24,000
    N = 400

  Therefore, there are 400 employees in the organization.

### Temperature: 8.0 | Problem 98 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: A man divides Rs 8600 among 5 sons, 4 daughters and 2 nephews. If each daughter receives four times as much as each nephew, and each son receives five as much as each nephew. How much does each daughter receive ?
Choices:
  A: Rs 400
  B: Rs 500
  C: Rs 600
  D: Rs 700
  E: Rs 800
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Let the share of each nephew be x.
  Each daughter receives four times as much as each nephew. Therefore, each daughter receives 4x.
  Each son receives five times as much as each nephew. Therefore, each son receives 5x.
  Total number of children = 5 sons + 4 daughters + 2 nephews = 11.
  Total amount = Rs 8600.
Thought:
  Let the share of each nephew be x.
  Each daughter receives 4x.
  Each son receives 5x.
  Total number of children = 11.
  Total amount = Rs 8600.
  Total share of nephews = 2x.
  Total share of daughters = 4 * 4x = 16x.
  Total share of sons = 5 * 5x = 25x.
  Total share of all children = 2x + 16x + 25x = 43x.
  43x = 8600.
  Therefore, x = 200.
  Each daughter receives 4x = Rs 800.
  The answer is E: Rs 800.
Criticism:
  There are no flaws in the logic and reasoning used to solve this problem.
Action: Answer("E")

  Total number of daughters = 4
  Total number of sons = 5

  The cab charges $3.50 for the first quarter-mile and 10 cents for each additional quarter-mile.
Thought:
  The first quarter-mile costs $3.50, so we have $5 to spend on additional quarter-miles.
  We know that each additional quarter-mile costs 10 cents, which is equivalent to $0.10.
  We can divide $5 by $0.10 per quarter-mile to get the total number of additional quarter-miles we can travel.
  $5 / $0.10 per quarter-mile = 50 quarter-miles
  Therefore, the maximum distance we can travel is 50 quarter-miles plus the initial quarter-mile, which is 51 quarter-miles.
  One mile is equivalent to four quarter-miles (since there are 4 quarter-miles in a mile).
  Therefore, the maximum distance we can travel is 51 quarter-miles divided by 4 quarter-miles per mile, which is 12.75 miles.
  The answer is B: 12.75 miles.

  3.50 + 0.10(x - 1) <= 8.50
  0.10(x - 1) <= 5
  x - 1 <= 50
  x <= 51
